[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/faq#access)

Access
-----------------------------------------------------------------------

How do I get access?

1

[](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/faq#)

First Step

Sign up to any plan on [our website](https://luxalgo.com/)
.

2

[](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/faq#)

Second Step

After purchasing a subscription, you will be prompted to **connect your accounts** & get instant access.

3

[](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/faq#)

Third Step

If you are having trouble, let our live human support team know your TradingView username and we will fix your access. If you’re speaking to an AI Agent, request to speak to a human directly.

Which plan should I choose?

The **Premium Plan** gives you the full set of our world-renowned Price Action Concepts®, Signals & Overlays®, and Oscillator Matrix® toolkits + screeners on TradingView which makes it the best choice for advanced technical analysis.The **Ultimate Plan** was designed for using our AI Backtesting platform and Backtesters, allowing you to automate backtesting of our toolkits. This is the most popular choice as it uses AI & deep optimization to give you the biggest advantage possible for data-driven, automated analysis.

Why don't I have access?

Make sure the username you used to connect your TradingView account is correct. If so, **refresh your browser/app** and then check your your Indicators —> Invite-only scripts folder on TradingView again.If you just created a TradingView account as you signed up for a LuxAlgo core platform subscription, it may take 5 - 10 minutes to be indexed in TradingView’s userbase first. Please wait and then try entering your username again within our Connect Accounts user portal.![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/faq/image521.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9d447532b351ef8ae93a746da2c9749d)If you still don’t have access, let our live human support team know your TradingView username and we will fix your access. If you’re speaking to an AI Agent, request to speak to a human directly.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/faq#products)

Products
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

What markets & timeframes do LuxAlgo exclusive tools work on?

Our tools are designed to work across all major asset classes and timeframes, but the specific coverage depends on which platform you are using:TradingView Indicators (Premium Plan): These tools function on any ticker and timeframe available on TradingView. Whether you are trading obscure altcoins, penny stocks, or futures on a 1-minute chart, the indicators will load and provide analysis instantly.LuxAlgo AI (Ultimate Plan): Our AI platform scans and backtests strategies on major liquid markets including Crypto (BTC, ETH, SOL, etc.), Forex (EURUSD, GBPUSD, etc.), Indices (SPX, NDX), and major Stocks. It is optimized for standard timeframes (5m, 15m, 1H, 4H, Daily) to find the most robust strategies for Scalping, Swing Trading, or Day Trading.

Do your indicators repaint?

No, all features within our toolkits do **not** repaint. Everything appears in real-time and are confirmed & permanent on the chart once the candle a signal was generated on has closed.Repainting is where past results of an indicator or a signal change based on data in the future. In terms of our exclusive tools, none of them repaint in any way. Only a small few of our hundreds of free indicators have this functionality.

When is a signal confirmed?

Within our Signals & Overlays toolkit, any signal is confirmed only once the candle is closed. This means a signal could appear on your chart but not be confirmed until that candle is closed and the next candle has started.Our alerts in Discord will **never** notify you on any signal until the candle has closed and confirmed it. If you’re adding alerts for our toolkits within TradingView, make sure to always select the “Once per bar close” configuration.

Do I need to pay for TradingView to use LuxAlgo?

You don’t need to upgrade your TradingView account, our exclusive tools work with 100% functionality on the basic plan of TradingView (free). [You can sign up for free here](https://www.tradingview.com/gopro/?share_your_love=LuxAlgo)
.

Are LuxAlgo paid plans friendly for beginners?

Yes, all of our plans are great for beginners.Every plan comes with many tutorials as well as access to our highly active community where users can get 24/7 support, discuss strategies, & go through daily analysis amongst each other using LuxAlgo.Our Ultimate Plan is great for traders who want to do more powerful strategy creation but even a beginner can maximize their advantage of it using our AI platform.

Can I automate my trades with LuxAlgo?

Yes, you can automate your trades using LuxAlgo. Our LuxAlgo AI platform is specifically designed for algorithmic trading, allowing you to generate backtested strategies and stream live signals directly to third-party automation platforms via webhooks.Additionally, our indicators and strategies available on TradingView can be automated in the same way by setting up alerts that trigger webhooks. However, for the most robust experience, we recommend using our AI strategies which are engineered specifically for generating automated signals.

Can I use LuxAlgo on MetaTrader (MT4 or MT5)?

Yes, you can send trades to MetaTrader via third parties.While our premium visual indicators (like Signals & Overlays™) are designed exclusively for the TradingView charting interface, you can still execute trades on your MT4 or MT5 account using our tools:For Automation (Recommended): You can use the LuxAlgo AI platform to generate strategies and stream signals directly to third party apps that plug in to your MetaTrader account via webhooks. This allows you to run algorithmic strategies on our platform while the trades execute automatically on yours.For Manual Trading: Many users perform their analysis on TradingView using our premium toolkits and then manually enter the resulting trades into their MetaTrader terminal.

Can I see every indicator in real-time data?

Yes, TradingView supports real-time data for the majority of tickers you can find on the platform. Only a small portion of them (mostly futures contracts) require a small monthly fee to access real-time data.

How are the paid tools better than the free LuxAlgo indicators?

While we are proud to be the world’s largest provider of free open-source indicators on TradingView, our paid plans offer a completely different level of professional capability:LuxAlgo AI (Ultimate): The biggest difference is our AI platform, which goes beyond simple indicators. It allows you to generate backtested strategies, optimize settings using data-driven insights, and automate your trading via webhooks—capabilities that do not exist in free scripts.Premium Toolkits: Our paid indicators (like Signals & Overlays and Price Action Concepts) are designed as “all-in-one” systems with extreme capabilities for customization & alert functionalities. Instead of combining multiple free indicators that clutter your chart, these toolkits provide comprehensive, noise-free workflows with advanced features and customization specifically engineered for serious traders.

Why am I getting 'Study\_not\_auth' error?

This error message appears when an user does not have access to the indicator. If you’ve already registered your TradingView username within our Connect Accounts portal and you’re seeing this message, refresh your browser or app and make sure you’re logged in on the TradingView profile you entered.If you are still getting this issue, let our live human support team know your TradingView username and we will fix your access. If you’re speaking to an AI Agent, request to speak to a human directly. If you have not signed up with us, you’ll see this error when trying to add our exclusive tools to your chart. You can get instant access [here](https://luxalgo.com/pricing)
.

Why am I getting 'Internal Server Study' error?

This error generally occurs when TradingView can’t handle script loads under high traffic. This error can appear when a high number of features are enabled. Changing settings within the indicators, or hiding/unhiding it will make the script recalculate and potentially fix the issue.We are always trying to improve the performance of the toolkit in order to limit these issues.

Why am I getting 'Memory limits exceeded. The study allocates X times more than allowed' error?

This error generally occurs when a TradingView study exceeds the memory limit fixed by TradingView. This error can’t be directly prevented and will generally be returned when using anything below the 1 minute timeframe.We recommend users to stay with minute and higher timeframes to avoid potential errors with our premium toolkits.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/faq#billing)

Billing
-------------------------------------------------------------------------

How do I cancel?

You can cancel your subscription anytime by logging directly into your account on [our website](https://luxalgo.com/account/)
 and accessing the billing page where you will find your subscription and a way to easily cancel it on your own.Once your subscription has been canceled, you will have access for the rest of the time in the plan you purchased and you will not be charged again.

How do I reactivate my subscription?

You can re-activate a subscription that you previously cancelled by purchasing a plan again on our [pricing page](https://luxalgo.com/pricing)
.Once you select the plan you want to subscribe back with, make sure to login to the same account you used with your previous subscription.

How do I upgrade my subscription?

You can upgrade your subscription by logging in on [our website](https://luxalgo.com/pricing)
.Once logged in, select your plan of choice to upgrade to and you will see a pop-up modal with the details.We automatically convert any remaining time into a value of days on your new plan so you have a longer period of time on your newly upgraded subscription.

How can I extend my current subscription plan?

You can extend your current subscription up to 3 times on [our website](https://luxalgo.com/pricing)
.Keep in mind that we only allow extending a subscription 3 times and it is for annual plans only.

How do discounts work?

For special limited time offers we do you can receive discounts which are all automatically applied, displayed on the pricing cards, and for the first payment of your subscription only.You can always get up to 50% off the total price you’d pay monthly by choosing to pay annually on our plans.

Is there a free trial?

We offer a 30 day money back guarantee so you can try our exclusive tools for 30 days risk free. We also have hundreds of free indicators you can try on our [Library](https://luxalgo.com/library)
 to experience our free tools first.

Will the price of my subscription ever change?

No, the price you signed up for is the price you will keep forever as long as you stay signed up. We will **never** change the price of your subscription. All members are grandfathered into the price they first signed up at regardless of any price increases we may do in the future.Please keep in mind that all coupons used on LuxAlgo.com are for the first interval of your subscription only. All future billing intervals aside from the first one will be at the full price of the subscription you chose.

How long does it take to get access after purchasing?

Access is instant for both our AI platform and TradingView tools immediately after sign-up:LuxAlgo AI Platform: You can log in directly on our website to access the AI strategies immediately.Complimentary TradingView tools: You will be prompted to enter your TradingView username in our Connect Accounts portal. Once connected, our Premium toolkits will instantly appear in your TradingView account under the “Invite-only scripts” folder (found within the Indicators menu on TradingView).Troubleshooting: If you don’t see the indicators on TradingView right away, try refreshing your browser or app. If you are still having trouble, please use the Live Chat on our website (request to speak to a human) or reply to your confirmation email, and our team will resolve it immediately.

What is your refund policy?

If you’re within 30 days of your first initial purchase, you can request a refund by getting in touch with our live human support team from contacting [\[email protected\]](https://docs.luxalgo.com/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#dba8aeababb4a9af9bb7aea3bab7bcb4f5b8b4b6)
 or by requesting to speak to a human if you’ve already reached out on our website so a team member can help you with this directly.

How do downgrades work?

Within your account, you can optionally downgrade your plan which will only start once your current plan ends.For example if you have 15 days left in your Ultimate Plan and you’re downgrading to Premium, the Premium plan will start in 15 days at full price.

Can I switch access to a different TradingView account?

Yes, we allow username changes in most scenarios as long as it’s not too frequent. You may request this and send your new username alongside your old username to [\[email protected\]](https://docs.luxalgo.com/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#4734323737283533072b323f262b20286924282a)
 and you may need to ask for our live human support team and we will change your username. If you’re speaking to an AI Agent, request to speak to a human directly for this request.

# Intro | Signals & Overlays Screener | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/screeners/s-o/introduction#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Screener (S&O)

Introduction

On this page

*   [Tickers](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/screeners/s-o/introduction#tickers)
    
*   [Display](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/screeners/s-o/introduction#display)
    
*   [Notes](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/screeners/s-o/introduction#notes)
    
*   [Computation](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/screeners/s-o/introduction#computation)
    
*   [Inconsistency](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/screeners/s-o/introduction#inconsistency)
    

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/screeners/s-o/introduction/screener.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=68043573d3882e9dc7a08b3386beeae1) The Screener (S&O) is a useful tool able to return recent information from various features in the **Signals & Overlays®** toolkit for up to 10 user set tickers with customizable timeframe. In order to use the screener the best way possible it is first advised to fully understand the [Signals & Overlays®](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/introduction)
 toolkit.

Provided below are pages describing all key features included.

Elements
--------

Filtering
---------

Sorting
-------

Having access to the **Signals & Overlays®** will automatically grant you access to the S&O screener.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/screeners/s-o/introduction#tickers)

Tickers
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Users can change tickers as well as their respective timeframes from the screener settings. Default tickers include:

*   BTCUSDT
*   ETHUSDT
*   SOLUSDT
*   ADAUSDT
*   SPX
*   AAPL
*   TSLA
*   NVDA
*   EURUSD
*   GBPUSD

The default timeframe used for all is the user chart timeframe. Supported tickers includes all tickers available on Tradingview (note that this availability can be affected by your Tradingview plan). Users can also use the same ticker but different timeframes, allowing to perform multi timeframe analysis of the **Signals & Overlays®** toolkit. However, duplicated tickers with the same timeframe will result in the duplicate ticker to not appear on the screener.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/screeners/s-o/introduction#display)

Display
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Users are offered a high degree of freedom when it comes to the placement of the screener. By default, the screener is located on a different pane, with the options to select the following positions:

*   Top Center
*   Top Right
*   Top Left
*   Bottom Center
*   Bottom Right
*   Bottom Left

It is also common for more compact screeners to be directly on the price chart, this is possible with this screener by drag and dropping it to the user chart, or by moving it to the existing pane above assuming the screener is in a pane below the price chart. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/screeners/pane.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=44d65f4c4c11edffb6d582b8717b402d)

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/screeners/s-o/introduction#notes)

Notes
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Tradingview is not a friendly environment when it comes to running more complete screeners, this cause various limitations showcased below:

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/screeners/s-o/introduction#computation)

Computation

The computation of a screener on Tradingview is very intensive, as such you can expect rare calculations timeouts. When this occurs simply force the screener recalculation by modifying one setting or adding the screener again to your chart.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/screeners/s-o/introduction#inconsistency)

Inconsistency

It is possible to observe inconsistencies when observing the screener on a chart with a specific symbol due to screener tickers having being on different market. The crypto market operates 24/7 while stock markets have opening and closing times, this can cause the screener to return different information when observing it from a cryptocurrency or stock/currency pair.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Pre-made Templates](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/readymade-scripts)
[Elements](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/screeners/s-o/elements)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Intro | Price Action Concepts Screener | LuxAlgo

Screener (PAC)

Introduction

# HyperWave Feature | Oscillator Matrix | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/hyperwave#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Oscillator Matrix

HyperWave

On this page

*   [Signal Line](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/hyperwave#signal-line)
    
*   [Turning Points](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/hyperwave#turning-points)
    
*   [Overbought/Oversold Turning Points](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/hyperwave#overbought%2Foversold-turning-points)
    
*   [Real Time Divergences](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/hyperwave#real-time-divergences)
    
*   [Divergences On Price Chart](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/hyperwave#divergences-on-price-chart)
    

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-oscillator/hyper-wave/settings.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=f1af1de610fd864e8179ef2c5d4ee7c6)

The HyperWave is a normalized adaptive oscillator aiming to precisely reflect price trends without returning a high amount of noise. It is the primary oscillator used to detect trends/reversals within the LuxAlgo Oscillator Matrix®. This oscillator is directly controlled by the **Main Length** setting, with higher values returning a smoother result reflecting longer term trends.

The HyperWave and every associated components (Signal line, turning points, divergences) can be disabled by toggling off “Show HyperWave”

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/hyperwave#signal-line)

Signal Line
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-oscillator/hyper-wave/signal.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=2201fba6ebcbee24742c79b75f0c88c5) The Hyper Wave includes a signal line allowing to reactively detect trend directions. The area between the Hyper Wave and its signal line is displayed to easily assess the current trend direction, with a color determined by the position of the Hyper Wave relative to its signal line. Users can use two different algorithms for computing the signal line:

*   SMA : A simple moving average of the Hyper Wave is used as signal line.
*   TS : A trailing stop of the Hyper Wave is used as signal line. This algorithm makes the signal line less sensitive to noisy variations of the Hyper Wave.

| SMA | TS  |
| --- | --- |
| ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-oscillator/hyper-wave/sma.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=006ee5b45d1834327086ab16c073ef84) | ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-oscillator/hyper-wave/ts.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=1cc3fd75f6016438696d77e141c5db1f) |

The users can select the length of the signal line using the numerical input at the right of the **Signal** drop-down menu.

It can be more interesting to use a higher signal line length when the **Main Length** setting is high.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/hyperwave#turning-points)

Turning Points
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-oscillator/hyper-wave/turning-points.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=eb197f09b3f5e411ccdd22573a28fedb) Crosses made between the HyperWave and its signal line are highlighted by dots on the oscillators pane, these are **turning points**. By default, a Hyper Wave crossing over the signal line is highlighted in green while a Hyper Wave crossing under the signal line is highlighted in red.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/hyperwave#overbought/oversold-turning-points)

Overbought/Oversold Turning Points

The displayed turning points exist in different sizes, with bigger dots occurring when the crosses are made within an overbought/oversold area.

*   Oversold Turning Point : Occurs when the Hyper Wave cross over its signal line while the Hyper Wave is under 20
*   Overbought Turning Point : Occurs when the Hyper Wave cross under its signal line while the Hyper Wave is over 80

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/hyperwave#real-time-divergences)

Real Time Divergences
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-oscillator/hyper-wave/divergences-settings.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=af66c965c28254c20547f09cd13323e6)

Divergences between the price and the HyperWave oscillator are detected in real-time. The users can return longer term divergences by decreasing the **Divergence Sensitivity %**, with lower values of this setting making divergence detection more sensitive to noisy variations of the Hyper Wave. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-oscillator/hyper-wave/divergences.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=13a5fe5a52fec1c2e9e0cf9b007650ca) Divergences are highlighted by a blue line for bullish divergences and by a red line for bearish divergences.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/hyperwave#divergences-on-price-chart)

Divergences On Price Chart

In order to reference the price points returning the divergence with the HyperWave, divergences lines are directly displayed on the user price chart thanks to “Show Divergences On Chart”. It is important to note that, unlike the divergence lines that appear in the oscillator pane, the divergence lines on the user chart do not appear exactly where the divergences are detected; rather, they are set retrospectively.

Because the amount of lines is limited to a maximum of 500, disabling “Show Divergences On Chart” can increase the amount of historical divergences highlighted on the oscillator pane.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Introduction](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/introduction)
[Smart Money Flow](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/smart-money-flow)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# TradingView Tutorial | How To Setup Alerts | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Get Started

TradingView Alerts

On this page

*   [How To Create An Alert](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#how-to-create-an-alert)
    
*   [Trigger Conditions](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#trigger-conditions)
    
*   [Crossing/Crossing Up/Crossing Down](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#crossing%2Fcrossing-up%2Fcrossing-down)
    
*   [Entering/Exiting Channel](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#entering%2Fexiting-channel)
    
*   [Outside/Inside Channel](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#outside%2Finside-channel)
    
*   [Greater/Less Than](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#greater%2Fless-than)
    
*   [How To Use Placeholders](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#how-to-use-placeholders)
    
*   [Warning Message](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#warning-message)
    
*   [Managing Alerts](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#managing-alerts)
    
*   [Updating Alerts](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#updating-alerts)
    

In this page, we show you the specifics of how to set up any alert on TradingView in general. If you want to learn how to set up specific alerts on our exclusive tools specifically, you can see the following [video](https://youtu.be/olKQq5XR5S0?t=38)
. On the TradingView platform, alerts can be created to trigger for any user set condition, such as crosses between two indicators, price entering or exiting a channel…etc. Users can be notified when the condition is trigerred via phone notifications, emails, SMS, and more through webhooks.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#how-to-create-an-alert)

How To Create An Alert
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To create an alert you can:

*   Click on the alert button at the top of your chart.

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/image510.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=3d02e4dc446c5b86e7cf8f44ea42a339)

*   From the alert manager

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/image370.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=3d928735e09edc6e063788cd607fac57)

*   Using hotkeys `ALT + A` (Windows) or `⌥ + A` (Mac)

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#trigger-conditions)

Trigger Conditions
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Users can select the conditions used to trigger an alert in the condition menu, selecting the indicators and a set of rules used to trigger an alert. The second drop down menu controls the specific alert trigger conditions, while the other drop down controls the elements/plots to be used for conditions.

Indicators return plots, which are visual elements that can be used to set the alert condition. Plots are used to visualize series of values, conditions, etc. Note that indicators can return multiple plots.

Available conditions to set custom alerts are explained below:

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#crossing/crossing-up/crossing-down)

Crossing/Crossing Up/Crossing Down

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/crossing_conditions.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=99fcea60ce209b16fb19a597a661659e) Crossing conditions are commonly used and allow users to be alerted when two elements cross each other. Three crossing conditions are available, **Crossing**, **Crossing Up**, **Crossing Down**. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/crossing.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=f927c555619b5af6efbec4d139b4b669) **Crossing** will alert on any crosses between two selected plots/values. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/crossingUp.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=d9895bb16b792a120c5089ed593efc0f) **Crossing Up** will alert only when the first selected element crosses over the second one. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/crossingDown.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=1c0d48dd4ce46c3d503948542b691dab) **Crossing Down** will alert only when the first selected element crosses over the second one.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#entering/exiting-channel)

Entering/Exiting Channel

**Entering/Exiting Channels** conditions will trigger when any selected element enter or exit user selected upper/lower bounds. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/enteringChannel.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=f0ac923d04d460612d0ca3419014eb0c) The **Entering Channel** condition will trigger when the element in the first drop-down menu cross-under the selected upper bound or cross-over the selected lower bound. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/exitingChannel.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=6f77484c2c6661cc96f69d89f3601ae0) The **Exiting Channel** condition will trigger when the element in the first drop-down menu cross-over the selected upper bound or cross-under the selected lower bound.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#outside/inside-channel)

Outside/Inside Channel

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/outsideChannel.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=19c328147822f5b09ab9599406d53f75) **Outside/Inside Channels** conditions will trigger when any selected element is outside or within selected upper/lower bounds. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/insideChannel.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=a3437986975e98ed0ddad0915b2befb5)

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#greater/less-than)

Greater/Less Than

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/greaterThan.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=3279b7ebd230609b0e45ee331f7091ca) The **Greater Than** and **Less Than** conditions will trigger when a selected element is greater or less than a selected element or value. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/lessThan.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=c5e696ce6efd686a4063224b5d0abd93)

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#how-to-use-placeholders)

How To Use Placeholders
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/image257.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=d1d4f1b1a4d97d8fcace8436f462e82f) Placeholders allow for the value of a variable to be returned in an alert message. This variable can be the closing price of a symbol (`{{close}}`), the time frame of the chart the alert is created on (`{{interval}}`), and even the value of an indicator. This is done using the `{{plot("Name")}}` placeholder, where `"Name"` is the name of the plot you want the value to be returned in the alert message. Note that only the first 22 plots in an indicator can be used in placeholders.

Note that `plot("Name")` must be part of the indicator selected in the alert condition.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#warning-message)

Warning Message
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/image276.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=5b993c561c4f04ed5abfb761b104cfdc) When you create an alert using certain indicators such as the Signals & Overlays® indicator, you might see a warning message, this is caused by internal Pinescript functions used in the script that may have a repainting behavior when set in a specific way. The alerts provided by the LuxAlgo indicators **do not repaint** and as such, you can click on **continue anyway**.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#managing-alerts)

Managing Alerts
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The alerts manager menu allows you to manage the alerts you have currently set. From there you can create, remove, pause, reactivate, clone, search, sort and edit your alerts. To access the alert manager menu click on the alerts icon represented by an alarm symbol at the top left of the chart. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/image370.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=3d928735e09edc6e063788cd607fac57) If you want to remove all your current alerts click on the three horizontal dots at the right of the “add alert” icon, then select “remove all”. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/image476.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=01258a61bd8c430cb9945f025ca94d10) For more information on how to manage alerts go [here](https://www.tradingview.com/support/solutions/43000595311-manage-alerts/)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts#updating-alerts)

Updating Alerts

It is important to note that if one of the indicator settings is **changed after the alert is created**, then the alert will be **triggered using the old settings**. In order to update an alert go to the alert manager and click on edit. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/image.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=6daed4ee8c861499618f63e676d617d6) In the first drop-down menu of the **Condition** section, select the second indicator with the same name as the one first used to create the alert you want to update and save the alert. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU/public/images/setup-alerts/image515.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=CDau_eRmDqLaKwqU&q=85&s=48aa844df2c3dc159ccfb4bb048adead)

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[How To Get Updates](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/how-to-update)
[FAQ](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/faq)

⌘I

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Premium & Discount | Price Action Concepts Toolkit | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/pdzones#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Navigation

Price Action Concepts

Premium & Discount Zones

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/zones/settings.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=219ccb6a90dcf8ac45be7e6f651fc246) Premium & Discount zones highlight three specific price areas, one upper area (premium), one central area (equilibrium), and one lower area (discount). ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/zones/premium-discount.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=52895a209ec2172d9944d0b1f7881354) These areas can be used to know when an event is occurring at a premium, discount, or within an equilibrium zone.

If a condition indicative of an uptrend occur within a discount zone then it would have an higher chance of being the cause of a reversal, this also applies for a condition indicative of a downtrend occurring within the premium zone.

Additionally, each area can be used as a support or resistance.

# Intro | Strategy Scripting Feature | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/introduction#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Strategy Scripting

Strategy Scripting

Strategy Scripting is a feature within each of our 3 Backtesters that allows users to create and backtests strategies using our own scripting language. This feature works just like [alert scripting](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/toolkits/alert-scripting/introduction)
 but is adjusted toward backtesting. To better learn about Strategy Scripting, see the following pages:

Placeholders
------------

Learn how to reference market and backtesting data when scripting strategies.

Operators
---------

Learn about the operators you can use to compare data with each other.

Actions
-------

Learn how to open, exit trades, and more using actions.

LUCID Connectors
----------------

Use any condition from any external LuxAlgo toolkit in your scripted strategy with LUCID connectors.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

*   [Examples](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#examples-8)
    

**Actions** are elements tied to a user set condition producing a specific effect when the assigned condition is true.

Actions have the structure `@keyword()`, starting with `@`, with an identifier, and `()`.Some actions can have a condition assigned to them using `=`. When the assigned condition is true the action will trigger.

Like functions in classical programming languages, actions can have arguments located within `()`, adding further degrees of control over the action. Actions used for scripted alerts are also available for scripted strategies, however, this page only lists the actions that are exclusively used for scripted strategies. To see a list of other actions, see [scripted alerts actions](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/toolkits/alert-scripting/actions-methods)

* * *

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#@long)

@long
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `@long` action allows entering a long position when the associated condition is true.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#syntax)

Syntax

    @long(limit, stop, alert_message)
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#arguments)

Arguments

**limit** (float): Optional. Limit price for the order. Accepts data placeholders as values. If specified, a limit order is created. **stop** (float): Optional. Stop price for the order. Accepts data placeholders as values. If specified, a stop order is created.

If both `limit` and `stop` are specified, a stop-limit order is created.

**alert\_message** (string): Optional. Alert message sent when the order is opened. Data placeholders can be used within the message, these will be replaced by their corresponding value when the alert triggers.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#examples)

Examples

    // Go long when the price is greater than the opening price
    @long() = {close} > {open}
    

    // Go long with a limit order at the previous high
    @long(limit = {high[1]}) = {close} > {open}
    

    // Go long with a stop order at the previous low
    @long(stop = {low[1]}) = {close} > {open}
    

    // Go long with a stop-limit order
    @long(limit = {high[1]}, stop = {low[1]}) = {close} > {open}
    

    // Go long with an alert message containing the entry price
    @long(alert_message = "Long entry at {close}") = {close} > {open}
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#remarks)

Remarks

By default a long position is entered at the opening of the next bar. Using “fill on bar close” from the settings in **PROPERTIES** → **FILL ORDERS** will open a position at the close of the bar the condition is true.

* * *

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#@short)

@short
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `@short` action allows entering a short position when the associated condition is true.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#syntax-2)

Syntax

    @short(limit, stop, alert_message)
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#arguments-2)

Arguments

**limit** (float): Optional. Limit price for the order. Accepts data placeholders as values. If specified, a limit order is created. **stop** (float): Optional. Stop price for the order. Accepts data placeholders as values. If specified, a stop order is created.

If both `limit` and `stop` are specified, a stop-limit order is created.

**alert\_message** (string): Optional. Alert message sent when the order is opened. Data placeholders can be used within the message, these will be replaced by their corresponding value when the alert triggers.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#examples-2)

Examples

    // Go short when the price is lower than the opening price
    @short() = {close} < {open}
    

    // Go short with a limit order at the previous low
    @short(limit = {low[1]}) = {close} < {open}
    

    // Go short with a stop order at the previous high
    @short(stop = {high[1]}) = {close} < {open}
    

    // Go short with a stop-limit order
    @short(limit = {low[1]}, stop = {high[1]}) = {close} < {open}
    

    // Go short with an alert message containing the entry price
    @short(alert_message = "Short entry at {close}") = {close} < {open}
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#remarks-2)

Remarks

By default a short position is entered at the opening of the next bar. Using “fill on bar close” from the settings in **PROPERTIES** -> **FILL ORDERS** will open a position at the close of the bar the condition is true.

* * *

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#@exit_long)

@exit\_long
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `@exit_long` action closes all open **long** positions when the associated condition is true.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#syntax-3)

Syntax

    @exit_long(qty, alert_message)
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#arguments-3)

Arguments

**qty** (float): Optional. Number of contracts/lots/shares/units to close on exit for a long position. If the character `%` is present, the specified % of the long position is closed. If not provied the entire position is closed. **alert\_message** (string): Optional. Alert message sent when the order is closed. Data placeholders can be used within the message, these will be replaced by their corresponding value when the alert triggers.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#examples-3)

Examples

    // Exit long position when price is below the price 14 bars ago
    @exit_long() = {close} < {close[14]}
    

    // Exit 50 contracts/lots/shares/units from the long position 
    // when price is below the price 14 bars ago
    @exit_long(50) = {close} < {close[14]}
    

    // Exit 50% of the long position 
    // when price is below the price 14 bars ago
    @exit_long(50%) = {close} < {close[14]}
    

    // Exit long position with an alert message containing the exit price
    @exit_long(alert_message = "Long exit at {close}") = {close} < {close[14]}
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#remarks-3)

Remarks

By default, a long position is exited at the opening of the next bar. You can enable “fill on bar close” from **PROPERTIES** → **FILL ORDERS** to trigger the exit at the bar close instead.

* * *

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#@exit_short)

@exit\_short
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `@exit_short` action closes all open **short** positions when the associated condition is true.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#syntax-4)

Syntax

    @exit_short(qty, alert_message)
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#arguments-4)

Arguments

**qty** (float): Optional. Number of contracts/lots/shares/units to close on exit for a short position. If the character `%` is present, the specified % of the short position is closed. If not provied the entire position is closed. **alert\_message** (string): Optional. Alert message sent when the order is closed. Data placeholders can be used within the message, these will be replaced by their corresponding value when the alert triggers.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#examples-4)

Examples

    // Exit short position when the high price is above previous low price
    @exit_short() = {high} > {low[1]}
    

    // Exit 50 contracts/lots/shares/units from the short position 
    // when the high price is above previous low price
    @exit_short(50) = {high} > {low[1]}
    

    // Exit 50% of the short position 
    // when the high price is above previous low price
    @exit_short(50%) = {high} > {low[1]}
    

    // Exit short position with an alert message containing the exit price
    @exit_short(alert_message = "Short exit at {close}") = {high} > {low[1]}
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#remarks-4)

Remarks

By default, a short position is exited at the opening of the next bar. To exit at the close of the bar where the condition is true, enable “fill on bar close” from **PROPERTIES** → **FILL ORDERS**.

* * *

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#@exit_all)

@exit\_all
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `@exit_all` action closes **all open positions** (long or short and scripted/unscripted) when the associated condition is true.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#syntax-5)

Syntax

    @exit_all()
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#examples-5)

Examples

    // Exit all positions when the closing price is above the previous high price
    @exit_all() = {close} > {high[1]}
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#remarks-5)

Remarks

This exits both scripted long and short positions, but also any other long/short condition you may have set.By default, the exit occurs at the next bar’s open unless “fill on bar close” is enabled in **PROPERTIES** → **FILL ORDERS**.

* * *

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#@start_date)

@start\_date
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `@start_date` action determines the starting date of the scripted strategy evaluation using a Datestring placeholder.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#syntax-6)

Syntax

    @start_date({YYYY-MM-DDThh:mm:ss±hh:mm})
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#arguments-5)

Arguments

**datestring**: Datestring placeholder, must comply with the ISO 8061 standard. The time and timezone are optional.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#examples-6)

Examples

    @long = {close} > {open}
    @short = {close} < {open}
    
    // Only evaluate the strategy starting 2025
    @start_date({2025-01-01})
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#remarks-6)

Remarks

The **Timezone** setting does not affect this placeholder. Default timezone for this placeholder is UTC-0.

* * *

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#@end_date)

@end\_date
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `@end_date` action determines the starting date of the scripted strategy evaluation using a Datestring placeholder.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#syntax-7)

Syntax

    @end_date({YYYY-MM-DDThh:mm:ss±hh:mm})
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#arguments-6)

Arguments

**datestring**: Datestring placeholder, must comply with the ISO 8061 standard. The time and timezone are optional.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#examples-7)

Examples

    @long = {close} > {open}
    @short = {close} < {open}
    
    // Only evaluate the strategy prior to 2025
    @end_date({2025-01-01})
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#remarks-7)

Remarks

The **Timezone** setting does not affect this placeholder. Default timezone for this placeholder is UTC-0.

* * *

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#@only_scripted)

@only\_scripted
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The `@only_scripted` action determines if only scripted entries/exits should be considered during the backtest. If `true` it will ignore any other entry condition set in the other Backtester settings.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#syntax-8)

Syntax

    @only_scripted()
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/actions#examples-8)

Examples

    // Only use the scripted strategy for the backtest
    @only_scripted() = true
    

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Placeholders](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/placeholders)
[LUCID Connectors](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/ai-backtesting/backtesters/strategy-scripting/lucid-connectors)

Price Action Concepts

Highs & Lows MTF

On this page

*   [Day of Week High / Low](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/previous-high-low#day-of-week-high-%2F-low)
    

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/YnBWCH3lJj52k-cF/public/images/lux-pa/previous-hl/settings.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=YnBWCH3lJj52k-cF&q=85&s=3b0ea3a415377a40af917712ff7e92b7) It is common for traders to use the maximum and minimum price point reached in a previous day, week, month, or on specific periods as support and resistances levels. Day of Week High / Low
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If the current day is the one selected, the returned level will track the highest and lowest prices reached during the day.

Some days of the week may be associated to closed markets for specific assets. As such certain days may not return levels when selected.

# How To Use | Alert Scripting | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

⌘KAsk AI

Navigation

Alert Scripting

Usage

On this page

*   [Building Simple Conditions](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#building-simple-conditions)
    
*   [Combining Conditions](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#combining-conditions)
    
*   [Combination using and](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#combination-using-and)
    
*   [Combination using or](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#combination-using-or)
    
*   [Sequencing and Steps](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#sequencing-and-steps)
    
*   [Invalidation](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#invalidation)
    
*   [Step Specific Invalidation](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#step-specific-invalidation)
    
*   [Invalidate on Step Evaluation Duration](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#invalidate-on-step-evaluation-duration)
    
*   [Visualizing Scripted Alerts Conditions](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#visualizing-scripted-alerts-conditions)
    
*   [Setting Scripted Alerts](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#setting-scripted-alerts)
    
*   [Comments](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#comments)
    

Alert scripting is a good way to create more complex alerts without feeling limited by the number of conditions or their limited reusability. This page covers the syntax of scripted alerts as well as showcasing typical use cases for alert scripting.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#building-simple-conditions)

Building Simple Conditions
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Users can define a simple condition over a single line in the text area “Condition Input Field”. In order to build effective conditions, we will need to reference specific data using [placeholders](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/placeholders)
 and compare this data with each other using [operators](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators)
. For example, we could define the following condition:

    {close} > {close[14]}
    

Here we have the following elements:

*   `{close}` placeholder, referencing the current closing price value
*   Greater than operator `>`, testing if the value to its left is greater than the value to its right
*   `{close[14]}` refer to the value of the closing price (`{close}`) 14 bars ago (defined by the historical referencing operator `[14]`)

This simple condition is `True` if the current closing price is higher than the closing price 14 bars ago.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#combining-conditions)

Combining Conditions

Creating slightly more complex conditions can involve combining individual ones into a single one, allowing us to retain more precise events or on the contrary, loosen our condition rules.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#combination-using-and)

Combination using `and`

Using the operator `and` allows to require more than one “sub-conditions” to be valid for the whole to be true. For example, we could reuse our previous condition but be more strict such that we only want to know when the current closing price is greater than the closing price 14 bars ago when it is between 1pm and 3pm (exchange timezone). To do this we can simply add another sub-condition leading to:

    {close} > {close[14]} and {hour} >= 13 and {hour} <= 15
    

`and` is similar to using the custom alert creator and having multiple enabled conditions using the same step number.

Another example where we can combine multiple conditions is to detect FVG’s, for the case of a bullish FVG we have the following requirements:

*   current low price is higher than the high price two bars ago
*   previous closing price is higher than the high price two bars ago

We can use alert scripting to detect bullish FVG’s from this combination of conditions as follows:

    {low} > {high[2]} and {close[1]} > {high[2]}
    

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#combination-using-or)

Combination using `or`

Sometimes we might be interested in getting alerted about two specific different conditions, without having to create two specific alerts. This is where `or` can be useful, requiring only one of the defined sub-conditions to be true in order for the alert to trigger. For example, we could want to be alerted either on a strong bullish confirmation signal, or when the Smart Trail turns bullish, this could be easily achieved using the following script:

    {bullish_confirmation+} or {bullish_smart_trail} and not {bullish_smart_trail[1]}
    

Here `{bullish_confirmation+}` is true when we have a strong bullish confirmation signal. `{bullish_smart_trail}` when the Smart Trail is bullish, with the whole `{bullish_smart_trail} and not {bullish_smart_trail[1]}` being true when the Smart Trail is currently bullish while the previous Smart trail is **not** bullish.

`or` takes precedence over `and`. You can think of this as a way to split a whole condition into multiple sub-conditions.For example if we have `{A} and {B} or {C} > 0 or {D} and {E}`, the precedence of or would split this conditions leading to `{A} and {B}`, `{C} > 0`, and `{D} and {E}`.Each of these individual sub-conditions would be evaluated individually, if one of them is true, then our whole condition is true.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#sequencing-and-steps)

Sequencing and Steps
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Users can create sequences of conditions, triggering an alert when the last step in a sequence is true. Sequences are constructed using the `then` operator, with each conditions seperated by `then` being a step. The first step is the leftmost one before `then`. When a step is valid, the next step condition will be evaluated at the next bar. Once the last step is evaluated and is true, the sequence is completed which can trigger an alert (if set) and will switch to the first defined step on the next bar.

This is similar in practice to how the custom alert creator works.

For example, we can define a sequence consisting of the following conditions:

*   Step 1: High price is lower than the previous high price
*   Step 2: Low price is lower than the previous low price
*   Step 3: Closing price is lower than the opening price

Leading to the following script:

    {my_sequence} = {high} < {high[1]} then {low} < {low[1]} then {close} < {open}
    

For clarity you can assign conditions over a single line to a UDP defined at the start.

    {condition1} = ...
    {condition2} = ...
    {condition3} = ...
    
    {my_sequence} = {condition1} then {condition2} then {condition3}
    

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#invalidation)

Invalidation

Invalidation refers to re-evaluating from the first step of a sequence of conditions when one or more specific conditions are true.

Invalidation takes place prior to evaluating steps.

Invalidation conditions can be defined for a sequence using the inline invalidation operator `!`:

    // Invalidate sequence when {close} is above {open}
    {my_sequence} = {high} < {high[1]} then {low} < {low[1]} then {close} < {open} ! {close} > {open}
    

If the condition after `!` is true, we go back to evaluating the sequence of conditions from step 1. Another way to perform invalidation is using the method `invalidate()`:

    // Invalidate sequence when {close} is above {open}, evaluate invalidation first
    {my_sequence}.invalidate() = {close} > {open}
    
    // Define sequence
    {my_sequence} = {high} < {high[1]} then {low} < {low[1]} then {close} < {open}
    

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#step-specific-invalidation)

Step Specific Invalidation

It is possible to apply invalidation conditions to specific steps, this is done using the `step` parameter in the `@invalidate` action. To illustrate this, we can reuse our previous sequence of conditions:

    {my_sequence} = {high} < {high[1]} then {low} < {low[1]} then {close} < {open}
    

Maybe that we don’t want the closing price to be greater than the opening price as long as the second step is the one being evaluated, this can be achieved as follows:

    {my_sequence} = {high} < {high[1]} then {low} < {low[1]} then {close} < {open} ! {close} > {open} and {my_sequence.step} == 1
    

Here `{my_sequence.step} == 1` refer to the second step of needing to be the one being evaluated in the sequence to apply the invalidation condition `{close} > {open}`.

With steps, 0 refers to the first step because it is 0 indexed.

Another way of doing this using the `invalidate` method can be done as follows:

    // Invalidate sequence 
    {my_sequence}.invalidate(step=1) = {close} > {open}
    
    // Define sequence
    {my_sequence} = {high} < {high[1]} then {low} < {low[1]} then {close} < {open}
    

Here `invalidate(step=1)` indicates that invalidation only takes place if the active step is the second one.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#invalidate-on-step-evaluation-duration)

Invalidate on Step Evaluation Duration

Sometimes we might not want to keep evaluating one or multiple steps for an excessive number of bars, and instead prefer having each step being triggered with a short interval in between. This can easily be done using invalidation and the placeholder `barssince_step`, which quantify the number of bars that elapsed since a step has started being evaluated or since invalidation took place. For example, we can invalidate a sequence of conditions if the amount elapsed since a step is greater than 5 bars:

    {my_sequence} = {high} < {high[1]} then {low} < {low[1]} then {close} < {open} ! {my_sequence.barssince_step} > 5
    

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#visualizing-scripted-alerts-conditions)

Visualizing Scripted Alerts Conditions
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/0Jdje6xa5PGD9ypH/public/images/alert-scripting/usage/highlight.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=0Jdje6xa5PGD9ypH&q=85&s=c981ba61d4dd732cb5cb6125102d9f6e) In order to make sure the scripted alert corresponds to the desired result and that it triggers as expected, users can visualize when the alert would have triggered using the “Highlight On Chart” setting. Enabling this setting will display a series of squares located at the top or bottom of the chart. When the last UDP condition specified in the script is true, the square will be colored in blue or the selected color from the setting.

Users can control the location of this highlighter on the chart trough the dropdown menu.“Top” and “Bottom” locations are available, while the Oscillator Matrix toolkit also includes a “Center” option.“None” will hide the scripted alert highlighting.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#setting-scripted-alerts)

Setting Scripted Alerts
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/0Jdje6xa5PGD9ypH/public/images/alert-scripting/usage/alert_toggle.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=0Jdje6xa5PGD9ypH&q=85&s=3983dab9ee8ec079ebbd9ba98e9d0b99) Once a scripted alert is defined, we can create an alert using it as a condition by enabling the “Scripted Alert” setting in the “Any alert() Function Call” settings group located at the bottom of the toolkit settings. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/0Jdje6xa5PGD9ypH/public/images/alert-scripting/usage/alert.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=0Jdje6xa5PGD9ypH&q=85&s=fee714fd65c37c3b6c8c2425a2a7511e) Then we can create the alert by clicking on the alert menu, selecting the toolkit in the condition dropdown, and making sure the dropdown below has “any alert() function call” selected. The alert will trigger whenever the last defined UDP condition is true.

More alerts can be created via scripting using the `@alert()` action, see [here](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/actions#@alert)
 for more information.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/usage#comments)

Comments
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To make a scripted alert easier to read, users can add comments by starting a line with `//`. Comments will be ignored when a scripted alert is evaluated. For example:

    // Step 1: candle color becomes green
    {barcolor} > 0 and not {barcolor[1]} > 0
    
    // Step 2: candle color is red
    {barcolor} < 0
    

Comments can also be set inline:

    // Step 1: candle color becomes green
    {green_color} = {barcolor} > 0 and not {barcolor[1]} > 0 
    
    @label() = {green_color} // Label when candle color becomes green
    

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Actions & Methods](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/actions-methods)
[Pre-made Templates](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/readymade-scripts)

⌘I

# Liquidity Features | Price Action Concepts Toolkit | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/liquidity#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Price Action Concepts

Liquidity Concepts

On this page

*   [Liquidity Trendlines](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/liquidity#liquidity-trendlines)
    
*   [Patterns](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/liquidity#patterns)
    
*   [Equal Highs & Lows](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/liquidity#equal-highs-%26-lows)

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/liquidity/settings.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=85fdd600db2f937c17597b93081ea864) Price Action Concepts® covers a variety of concepts related to liquidity. Each of these concepts can be found in the **Liquidity Concepts** settings section and are described in the sections below.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/liquidity#liquidity-trendlines)

Liquidity Trendlines
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/liquidity/trendlines.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=30284dd7e17189351d9db34e76001cbb) Liquidity Trendlines displays linear zones constructed by taking into account the amount of liquidity at certain price levels, with zones being displayed only if market participants found liquidity in them. The returned zones can give support areas (in blue) during up-trends or resistance areas (in red) during down-trends. Once price breaks the extremity of a zone we can expect a trend reversal.

Once the conditions for a trendline to be displayed are met, the indicator will display it retrospectively.

The user can determine the amount of historical up-trendlines and down-trendlines to display on the chart to avoid clutter using the provided numerical input setting.

Builtins alerts for trendlines breakouts are available to the users.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/liquidity#patterns)

Patterns
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/liquidity/image530.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=059c8e221d1c0f52323aafe06d2cd24a) Price Action Concepts® includes an Automatic Pattern Detection feature able to detect various chart patterns as well as a dashboard to give users information about any detected pattern. The Pattern Detection feature is able to detect the following patterns:

*   Ascending/Descending Triangles
*   Ascending/Descending Broadening Wedges
*   Ascending/Descending/Symmetrical Triangles
*   Double Tops/Bottoms
*   Head & Shoulders
*   Inverted Head & Shoulders

as well as providing general supports and resistances if any of the above patterns are not detected. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/liquidity/dashboard.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=6a141c02451d100beeab6920f6dc1089) When a pattern is detected, it will be displayed on the dashboard located at the top-right of the chart. Solid lines will highlight the patterns. When no patterns are detected, dashed lines will be displayed that can be used as support and resistance. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/liquidity/image602.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=b379be3fab6812dd10c24582cb26985c) Users can detect longer term chart patterns using the provided numerical drop-down menu setting, with higher values detecting longer term patterns.

Builtins alerts for detected patterns are available to the users.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/liquidity#equal-highs-&-lows)

Equal Highs & Lows
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/liquidity/eqhl.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=e93734e23fa38cd95bd91f352cfa2f02) The toolkit returns historical equal high’s & low’s constructed from swing points. Equal high’s & low’s can be indicative of reversals, and incoming market structure such as CHoCH or BOS. Users can display longer term equal high’s/low’s by increasing the numerical input at the right of the toggle (3 by default).

Equal high’s & low’s requires the detected swing points to be confirmed, which takes an amount of bars equal to the value set in the numerical input. As such it is important to understand these are displayed retrospectively.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/liquidity#liquidity-grabs)

Liquidity Grabs
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/liquidity/grabs.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=2a8e76e1cf7ccb125f19af7ccdc823a8) Liquidity Grabs highlight occurrences where trading activity took place in more liquid areas. These are highlighted by the toolkit with colored borders. A liquidity grab can be identified as a bullish grab if the activity took place in a demand area, or a bearish grab if this activity took place in a supply area. Bullish liquidity grabs are highlighted in blue with borders ranging from the price low to candle body minimum and indicates a potential bullish reversal. Bearish liquidity grabs are highlighted in red with borders ranging from the price high to candle body maximum and indicates a potential bearish reversal. The occurrence of both bullish and bearish liquidity grabs at the same time can highlight market indecision’s.

Built-in alerts for liquidity grabs are available to users within Price Action Concepts®.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

# Candle Coloring | Signals & Overlays | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/candle-coloring#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Signals & Overlays

Candle Coloring

On this page

*   [Confirmation Simple](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/candle-coloring#confirmation-simple)
    
*   [Confirmation Gradient](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/candle-coloring#confirmation-gradient)
    
*   [Contrarian Gradient](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/candle-coloring#contrarian-gradient)
    

The candle coloring feature allows the user to change the body color of the candles/bars when using candlesticks or bar charts. Three coloring modes are available, with two of them being based on the previously described signal methodologies. Candle coloring also works on charts using Heikin-Ashi, Renko, Kagi, line break, point and figure, and range candles. Each mode can be enabled from the settings in the **candle color mode** dropdown menu. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/candle-coloring/image547.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=e0722683dde7d7e26e3518b8c1f75c7c) In order to use candle coloring as properly as possible make sure to disable the **borders** setting in your chart settings. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/candle-coloring/image72.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=5868c46c261272b1316309e8f038c385)

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/candle-coloring#confirmation-simple)

Confirmation Simple

The **confirmation simple** color mode is based on the methodology used by confirmation signals and is the one enabled by default. This mode uses three colors, each one can be interpreted as follows:

*   **Green candles:** Strong bullish signal active.
*   **Red candles:** Strong bearish signal active.
*   **Purple candles:** Normal bullish or bearish signal active.

![Confirmation Simple color mode](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/candle-coloring/image398.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=3ce26e90f3dde1d25dd5ff37dad0a9b2)

If you need to set an alert based on candle coloring or need to return information on what is the current candle color on an alert message simply use the **Bar Color Value** variable. This variable as three possible values each indicating the following:

*   1: Candle color is green
*   0: Candle color is purple
*   \-1: Candle color is red

This variable can be used as input for external indicators as well.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/candle-coloring#confirmation-gradient)

Confirmation Gradient

The **confirmation gradient** color mode is also based on the algorithm that generates confirmation signals, but will slightly differ from the previously described **confirmation simple** color mode. Lighter green colors indicate strong bullish variations, while lighter red colors indicate strong bearish variations. Colors closer to purple indicate that the current variation might be a retracement or that the market is ranging. ![Confirmation Gradient color mode](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/candle-coloring/image93.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=d9ab58396e1c120df64636d40e5f9cb1)

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/candle-coloring#contrarian-gradient)

Contrarian Gradient

The **contrarian gradient** color mode is based on the contrarian signals algorithm. Stronger green colors indicate an oversold market and a potential reversal, while stronger red colors indicate an overbought market. ![Contrarian Gradient color mode](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/candle-coloring/contrarian.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=3cab6d944402cd08bb311d910f6a94cb)

Was this page helpful?

[Dashboard](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/dashboard)
