# Indicator Overlays | Signals & Overlays | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/indicator-overlay#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Signals & Overlays

Indicator Overlay

On this page

*   [Smart Trail](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/indicator-overlay#smart-trail)
    
*   [Reversal Zones](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/indicator-overlay#reversal-zones)
    
*   [Trend Tracer](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/indicator-overlay#trend-tracer)
    
*   [Trend Catcher](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/indicator-overlay#trend-catcher)
    
*   [Neo Cloud](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/indicator-overlay#neo-cloud)
    

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/indicator-overlay/image634.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=f19fb5c71c97323c685164230b6196cd) Signals & Overlays® Indicator allows the user to display various technical indicators directly on their chart. These can be used in confluence with the confirmation/contrarian signals or optionally used as a standalone. Each overlay has an associated setting affecting its output. These settings range from 1 to 5, with higher values allowing the overlay to return indications for longer-term trends.

All overlays use a default sensitivity of 3 except the Neo Cloud which uses a sensitivity of 2.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/indicator-overlay#smart-trail)

Smart Trail
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-algo/indicator-overlay/smart.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=ef225df5afd92cb6ece9b3941b04bee0) The Smart Trail is a trailing stop that diverges from the price in the presence of unwanted price variations in a trend. An up-trend is indicated when the price is above the trailing stop, and a down-trend when the price is below the trailing stop. The Smart Trail also displays support (in blue) and resistance (in red) areas and aims to indicate when the price might reverse when entering the area.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/indicator-overlay#reversal-zones)

Reversal Zones
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When enabled, one upper and one lower zone will be displayed on your chart, each zone is designed to help the user find tops and bottoms whether the market is ranging or trending (however the indicator will still be more effective during ranging markets). ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/indicator-overlay/reversal.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=93e7660371c50ea28c3c4ccff18fb27d) These zones can be great areas to take profit or find early entries to use alongside the confirmation or contrarian signals.

During periods of increased volatility, the price may move outside the zones, you can wait for the price to go back within each zone to take a decision.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/indicator-overlay#trend-tracer)

Trend Tracer
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-algo/indicator-overlay/tracer.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=9206988b2f20dfac77714f1e20c5f5de) The Trend Tracer is a trend-following algorithm that aims to estimate the underlying trend in the price. When the indicator indicates an uptrend its color will be blue, while orange in the case of a downtrend.

The Trend Tracer can be used as a trailing support/resistance tool, you can also use it in confluence with the confirmation signals, either by waiting for the price to reach the trend tracer in order to enter a trade corresponding to the current confirmation signal or by filtering shorter-term signals by only trading those in accordance by the trend estimated by the trend tracer.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/indicator-overlay#trend-catcher)

Trend Catcher
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/indicator-overlay/catcher.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=15141d000fe84d0b05fc55a833c6c4c5) The Trend Catcher is a similar algorithm to the previous **Trend Tracer**, however, it aims to detect very early trends, and is thus more reactive. Like with the **Trend Tracer**, the color of the indicator determines the detected trend.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/indicator-overlay#neo-cloud)

Neo Cloud
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/indicator-overlay/neo.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=d349a5f44149ebf3befd836d085b827c) When enabled, a simple cloud-like indicator will be displayed on your chart. The Neo Cloud is similar in effect to the Ichimoku Cloud, and can determine the current trend direction. The cloud is filled with a gradient color showing how new a detected trend is, with brighter colors indicating older trends. This cloud can provide a support when an uptrend is detected or resistance when a downtrend is detected. This makes it perfect for entries into precise trades.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[TP/SL Points](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/tp-sl-points)

# Imbalances | Price Action Concepts Toolkit | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Price Action Concepts

Imbalance Concepts

On this page

*   [Fair Value Gaps](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#fair-value-gaps)
    
*   [Inverse FVG](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#inverse-fvg)
    
*   [Double FVG](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#double-fvg)
    
*   [Volume Imbalance](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#volume-imbalance)
    
*   [Opening Gap](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#opening-gap)
    
*   [Mitigation Methods](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#mitigation-methods)
    
*   [Volatility Threshold](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#volatility-threshold)
    
*   [Alerts](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#alerts)
    

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/imbalances/settings.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=a0cf80ecf3f70e44fb82cd2d02369939) Imbalances in market prices arise when there is a great disparity between supply and demand, this can lead to inefficiencies where an asset does not trade at its fair value. It is common for the price to seek balance after an imbalance, thus returning to the price area where the imbalance occurred. These areas of imbalances can also be used as support and resistance areas. The toolkit is able to detect the following imbalances:

*   Fair Value Gaps (FVG)
*   Inverse Fair Value Gaps (Inverse FVG)
*   Double Fair Value Gaps (Double FVG)
*   Volume Imbalance
*   Opening Gap

Each method is covered in the sections below.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#fair-value-gaps)

Fair Value Gaps
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-pa/imbalances/fvg.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=5f56c1f3f9ccc02cccecd36db4ecf634) Fair Value Gaps (FVG) are market imbalances formed from a sequence of three candles where the outer candle wicks fail to overlap the central candle body, the range between the wicks highlight a Fair Value Gap. Bullish fair value gaps occur when the current price low is higher than the price high two bars ago. Bearish fair gaps occur when the current price high is lower than the price low two bars ago.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#inverse-fvg)

Inverse FVG
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-pa/imbalances/ifvg.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=09aed8cefdb4b92794b5aae32f4b7d18) Inverse fair value gaps are essentially mitigated fair value gaps, these can be used to provide retests areas. A mitigated bullish FVG will lead to a bearish inverse FVG, where we can expect price to retrace upward and retest the area, while a mitigated bearish FVG will lead to a bullish inverse FVG, where we can expect price to retrace downward and retest the area.

For the sake of efficiency, inverse FVG’s are always based on the mitigation of the most recent detected FVG, disregarding any previous historical FVG that might get mitigated.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#double-fvg)

Double FVG
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-pa/imbalances/bpr.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=25558fe00da3cbccc555f3fecccf8078) Double Fair Value Gaps, also called balanced price ranges occur when the areas of two Fair Value Gaps overlap. The overlapping areas highlight a new area of imbalance. A bullish Balanced Price Range is determined by a new bullish Fair Value Gap area overlapping a previous bearish Fair Value Gap area, while a bearish Balanced Price Range is determined by a new bearish Fair Value Gap area overlapping a previous bullish Fair Value Gap area.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#volume-imbalance)

Volume Imbalance
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/imbalances/vi.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=b735263f99733c442518e7330f85fcf5) Volume Imbalances are market imbalances characterised by two adjacent candles with non overlapping candle bodies, while their wicks overlaps. These imbalances are more commonly found in stocks or second timeframes of cryptocurrencies and forex pairs.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#opening-gap)

Opening Gap
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/imbalances/og.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=2d001ccaf4b007215b22e84d8e7ab5e2) Opening Gaps are market imbalances characterised by two adjacent candles with non overlapping candle wicks, highlighting an empty area. These imbalances are more commonly found in stocks or second timeframes of cryptocurrencies and forex pairs.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#mitigation-methods)

Mitigation Methods
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Once price breaks a highlighted imbalance area it is said to have been “mitigated” and will automatically disappear. Within the Price Action Concepts® indicator, users can determine the condition for any imbalance to be considered mitigated trough the **Mitigation Method** setting, available options include:

| Method | Description |
| --- | --- |
| **Close** | Mitigates an imbalance once price close cross above the imbalance upper extremity in the case of a bearish imbalance, and under its lower extremity in case of a bullish imbalance. |
| **Wick** | Mitigates an imbalance once price high cross above the imbalance upper extremity in the case of a bearish imbalance, and when price low cross under its lower extremity in case of a bullish imbalance. |
| **Average** | Mitigates an imbalance once price cross the imbalance area average level. |
| **None** | Will not remove mitigated imbalances. |

This toolkit makes use of a buffer allowing for a maximum of 200 imbalances. Any newly detected imbalance making the buffer exceed this number will cause the toolkit to discard the oldest detected imbalance.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#volatility-threshold)

Volatility Threshold
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The volatility threshold allows filtering out less significant imbalances, with higher values preserving imbalances with a larger range.

The volatility threshold is determined from a volatility estimator, the threshold act as a multiplier.Increments of 1 will return visible results. Floating points can be used.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/imbalances#alerts)

Alerts
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Users can be alerted on the detection of a bullish or bearish imbalance, as well as when an imbalance area is mitigated.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Premium & Discount Zones](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/pdzones)

# Fibonacci | Price Action Concepts Toolkit | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/fibonacci#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Price Action Concepts

Fibonacci Retracements

On this page

*   [Possible Extremities](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/fibonacci#possible-extremities)
    
*   [Ratios](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/fibonacci#ratios)
    
*   [Anchor To Origin](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/fibonacci#anchor-to-origin)
    

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/retracements/settings.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=c4f93b03657c3a9a1298e07be37412e0) Fibonacci retracements are levels displayed from two price points using Fibonacci ratios, specific numbers obtained from the Fibonacci sequence. Users can display up to 5 customizable Fibonacci retracements from one upper and one lower extremities users can select from a wide variety of feature included in the toolkit.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/fibonacci#possible-extremities)

Possible Extremities
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The upper/lower extremities used to construct the Fibonacci retracements can be selected from the “Fibonacci Top” or “Fibonacci Bottom” dropdown settings, and can be obtained from the following features within the Price Action Concepts® toolkit:

Swing Points

*   Internal High
*   Internal Low
*   Swing High
*   Swing Low

Premium/Discount

*   Discount
*   Equilibrium Average
*   Premium

CHoCH/BOS

*   Bullish I-CHoCH
*   Bearish I-CHoCH
*   Bullish I-BOS
*   Bearish I-BOS

Orderblock

*   Highest OB Top
*   Lowest OB Bottom

Imbalance

*   Imbalance Top
*   Imbalance Bottom
*   Imbalance Average

Previous H/L

*   Previous Day High
*   Previous Day Low
*   Previous Week High
*   Previous Week Low
*   Previous Month High
*   Previous Month Low
*   Previous Quarterly High
*   Previous Quarterly Low

Selecting “None” for “Fibonacci Top” or “Fibonacci Bottom” will hide the retracements.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/fibonacci#ratios)

Ratios
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/retracements/levels.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=2bc0542be1a0a0ca981c41462b847ee0) Users can control which levels are displayed as well as the ratio used for each level. Ratios are also visible to the right side of each retracement displayed.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/fibonacci#anchor-to-origin)

Anchor To Origin
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/retracements/origin.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=ace9e2dcf63e98d82aaf0f94da8cbbd4) By default, the levels are anchored from the most recent bar and extend 20 bars ahead. By enabling “Anchor To Origin” users can anchor retracement levels to a point of origin related to the selected extremities in “Fibonacci Top” and “Fibonacci Bottom”. Based on the selected extremity, the anchor point will be the following:

| Extremity | Anchor |
| --- | --- |
| Swing High | Swing High Location |
| Swing Low | Swing Low Location |
| Internal High | Internal High Location |
| Internal Low | Internal Low Location |
| Premium / Equilibrium Average / Discount | Oldest anchor between Swing High and Swing Low Locations |

Only the above extremities are compatible with “Anchor To Origin”.

If “Fibonacci Top” and “Fibonacci Bottom” are different, the anchor point will be the oldest location between the two.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Highs & Lows MTF](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/previous-high-low)
[Alerts](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/alerts)

# Market Structure | Price Action Concepts Toolkit | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Price Action Concepts

Market Structure

On this page

*   [Type Of Market Structures](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#type-of-market-structures)
    
*   [Change Of Character (CHoCH)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#change-of-character-choch)
    
*   [Break Of Structure (BOS)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#break-of-structure-bos)
    
*   [Swing & Internal Structure](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#swing-%26-internal-structure)
    
*   [Candle Coloring](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#candle-coloring)
    
*   [Swing High/Low](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#swing-high%2Flow)
    
*   [Strong/Weak High/Low](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#strong%2Fweak-high%2Flow)
    
*   [Alerts](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#alerts)
    

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/structures/settings.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=352ee6259e2379ba7272de77a00bb4c0) Market structure is a core component of the price action. The Price Action Concepts® toolkit automatically detects and highlights real time market structure on your chart, allowing for a clean picture of market trends without introducing traditional forms of technical analysis like moving averages.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#type-of-market-structures)

Type Of Market Structures
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![Type of market structures](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/structures/type-structures.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=52cc4029448299d08c1f3125d6796769) Market structure allows traders to understand trend reversals as well as trend continuations in the market through two distinct identifications:

*   Change of Character (CHoCH)
*   Break of Structure (BOS)

These are further described in the subsections below.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#change-of-character-choch)

Change Of Character (CHoCH)

![Type of CHoCH's](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/structures/CHoCH.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=668883850330af4b80081fa8e7352d7f) A change of character (CHoCH), sometimes also referred as ‘market structure shift’ is characterized by price breaking a prior swing low during an uptrend (bullish CHoCH) or a prior swing high during a downtrend (bearish CHoCH), and thus indicates a potential market reversal. The Price Action Concepts® toolkits labels two distinct type of CHoCHs:

*   Leading CHoCH (labelled as **CHoCH**)
*   Supported CHoCH (labelled as **CHoCH+**)

The difference between each is based on the relative position of prior swing highs/lows. A leading CHoCH is characterized by price not having prior signs of a reversal, such as a failed higher high (lower high) during an uptrend or a failed lower low (higher low) during a downtrend. On the other hand, a supported CHoCH (**CHoCH+**) is preceded by an early sign of market reversal, such as a failed higher high (lower high) during an uptrend or a failed lower low (higher low) during a downtrend.

Users can show allow the toolkit to show all or only specific types of CHoCH’s from the drop-down menus within the **Market Structure** settings section in the toolkit.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#break-of-structure-bos)

Break Of Structure (BOS)

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/structures/BOS.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=15f2281c7e7f42b60cdde5750ea741c7) A break of structure (BOS) can be thought of primarily as a trend continuation label. This structure is the opposite of the CHoCH, with a BOS being when price breaks a prior swing high during an uptrend (bullish BOS) thus forming a new higher high, or when price breaks a prior swing low during a downtrend (bearish BOS) thus forming a new lower low. This structure only can occur after a CHoCH. Since BOS’s indicate trend continuations, it is common to observe successive BOS’s.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#swing-&-internal-structure)

Swing & Internal Structure
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/structures/structures.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=d3a3fad2f0107c6c935a359fb0032029) The Price Action Concepts® toolkit offers two distinct dimensions when it comes to market structure:

*   Internal Structure
*   Swing Structure

Internal structure are constructed from shorter term swing high/low points, while swing structure are constructed from longer term ones. Users can select the lookback used for the swing point detection for both the internal and swing market structures construction. Internal structures can use a lookback in range (5, 49). Swing structures can use a lookback in the range (50, 100). The toolkit highlights internal structure with dashed lines and labels with a smaller text size.

The size of the labels for internal and swing structure can be changed from the **General Styling** settings section.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#candle-coloring)

Candle Coloring
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/structures/coloring.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=a2446f5ed01ddbadf8d35364e3c82fd8) Users can color candles depending on the detected internal market structure. This is useful if users want to be able to determine a detected internal market structure without having labels and lines on their chart, freeing up space on the chart to use other indicators. Candle coloring is affected by the colors settings selected by the user for the internal market structure. Candle coloring is determined as follows:

*   Darker bullish color : Bullish CHoCH active
*   Regular bullish color : Bullish BOS active
*   Darker bearish color : Bearish CHoCH active
*   Regular bearish color : Bearish BOS active

Users can make highlighted structure and candle colors monochrome from the **General Styling** settings by using the _monochrome_ option in the **Theme** drop down menu.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#swing-high/low)

Swing High/Low
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Users can display swing high/low by enabling the “Show Swing High/Low” setting, highlighting past points where a reversal occurred. Displayed swing points can be denoted as:

*   HH (Higher high)
*   HL (Higher low)
*   LH (Lower high)
*   LL (Lower low)

The displayed swing points are affected by the period selected for the internal market structures, with higher values returning longer term swing points.

Swing points are displayed retrospectively, and as such are not detected where they are located. They should not be used for real-time applications.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#strong/weak-high/low)

Strong/Weak High/Low
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX/public/images/lux-pa/structures/strongweak.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-_VCBHd2xJR0PihX&q=85&s=236c70579b18c5030d27bdff0224bed3) Strong/Weak High/Lows highlight maximum and minimum levels made from medium term swings. A relative percentage derived between the trading volume that occurred on both swings is also highlighted, and is used to determine if a maxima/minima is strong or weak. The displayed swing points are affected by the period selected for the internal market structures, with higher values returning longer term swing points.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/market-structures#alerts)

Alerts
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Built-in alerts are available for each supported market structure, including swing structures, internal structures, and equal highs/lows.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Introduction](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/introduction)
[Volumetric Order Blocks](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/price-action-concepts/order-blocks)

# Signal Settings | Signals & Overlays | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Signals & Overlays

Signal Settings

On this page

*   [Manual Adjustments](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#manual-adjustments)
    
*   [Confirmation Signals](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#confirmation-signals)
    
*   [Method For Manually Adjusting Confirmation Signals](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#method-for-manually-adjusting-confirmation-signals)
    
*   [Contrarian Signals](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#contrarian-signals)
    
*   [Automatic Settings Estimation](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#automatic-settings-estimation)
    
*   [Autopilot Signal Settings](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#autopilot-signal-settings)
    
*   [Dashboard Optimal Sensitivity](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#dashboard-optimal-sensitivity)
    
*   [Choosing The Right Method](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#choosing-the-right-method)
    
*   [Manual Adjustments](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#manual-adjustments-2)
    
*   [Automatic Adjustments](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#automatic-adjustments)
    

The settings affecting the signal generation algorithm within Signals & overlays plays an important role in using the signals effectively. We give our users the possibility to adjust the settings so that the signals can fit their trading style but we also provide ways to easily adjust settings by using a wide variety of methods. Each method for adjusting signal settings is designed to fit specific user needs, one method will not necessarily be more accurate than another.

It’s critical to understand Confirmation Signals are generally meant to be used as trend confirmations, not direct entries & exits. Focusing on ease of use with the signal settings & using other features within our toolkits will likely be the best decision for you rather than trying to find the “holy grail” of optimized signal settings & following the signals alone.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#manual-adjustments)

Manual Adjustments
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Manual adjustment of signals settings allow the user to fit the signals to their trading style and allows a greater degree of customizability.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#confirmation-signals)

Confirmation Signals

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-algo/signal-settings/image565.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=b07947b3e82134cadd640dcd692c29d2) Confirmation signals are affected by the **Signals Sensitivity** setting. Increasing this setting will allow the trader to make decisions for longer-term trends.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#method-for-manually-adjusting-confirmation-signals)

Method For Manually Adjusting Confirmation Signals

First, identify which price movements you are looking to trade (regardless of timeframes). Depending on how you are on your charts (on any timeframe) you can adjust the sensitivity value higher or lower to catch the price movements you are looking for. If you are looking for shorter term price movements on those timeframes, you should consider using a lower sensitivity. If you are looking for longer term price movements on those timeframes you should consider using a higher sensitivity.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#contrarian-signals)

Contrarian Signals

Contrarian signals are also affected by the **Signals Sensitivity** setting, increasing it will aim to make contrarian signals spot longer term tops and bottoms.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#automatic-settings-estimation)

Automatic Settings Estimation
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#autopilot-signal-settings)

Autopilot Signal Settings

The downside of adjusting signal settings is that this task needs to be constantly repeated due to ever-changing market conditions. **Autopilot** is a feature that allows the user to avoid adjusting signal settings completely. Instead, the currently selected signal generation algorithm (Confirmation or Contrarian) adjusts dynamically to the market conditions in order to provide the best signals possible. This setting can be enabled from the **Advanced Settings** settings section.

Compared to other automatic methods the “Autopilot” feature is the most user-friendly since it avoids adjusting inputs within the indicator entirely.

[](https://docs.luxalgo.com/public/images/lux-algo/signal-settings/autopilotfreq.png)
The **Autopilot Sensitivity** advanced setting allows autopilot to adjust to shorter or longer term trends depending on user preference.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#dashboard-optimal-sensitivity)

Dashboard Optimal Sensitivity

The Optimal Sensitivity is a value displayed on the Lux Dashboard showing the optimal **Sensitivity** setting when using Confirmation or Contrarian signal modes. This optimization is based on a grid search algorithm and as such will backtest every generated signals using a sensitivity ranging from 10 to 20 over the most recent 250 bars. This feature works on any ticker & timeframe as long as at least 250 bars of historical data are available.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#choosing-the-right-method)

Choosing The Right Method
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

While the optimal sensitivity provided by the dashboard is the most precise method since it’s performing grid search, there is no “best” method for optimizing signals as it’s up to the user to understand their style of trading and the price variations they want to trade (regardless of timeframes).

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#manual-adjustments-2)

Manual Adjustments

Do you specifically want to trade **shorter**\-term trends on the timeframes you use?

*   Consider using lower sensitivity values such as 5-10

Do you specifically want to trade **longer**\-term trends on the timeframes you use?

*   Consider using higher sensitivity values such as 20+

Alternatively, you can use the default of 12 for trading medium-term trends. This provides simple and responsive signals.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signal-settings#automatic-adjustments)

Automatic Adjustments

Do you rely a lot on optimizing signals and are you ok with updating these manually over time?

*   Use the Optimal Sensitivity provided by the dashboard to find more precise signal settings.

Do you completely dislike the process of adjusting signal settings altogether?

*   Use the Autopilot sensitivity to allow the signals to adjust dynamically and work without the need of any user interaction.

Using Autopilot or the default settings are overall the simplest user experience as it allows you to completely avoid adjusting settings altogether.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Signal Modes](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/signals)
[Indicator Overlay](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/indicator-overlay)

# Operators | Alert Scripting Feature | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Alert Scripting

Operators

On this page

*   [Comparison Operators](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#comparison-operators)
    
*   [\> (Greater Than)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#%3E-greater-than)
    
*   [< (Less Than)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#%3C-less-than)
    
*   [\>= (Greater Than or Equal)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#%3E%3D-greater-than-or-equal)
    
*   [<= (Less Than or Equal)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#%3C%3D-less-than-or-equal)
    
*   [\== (Equal)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#%3D%3D-equal)
    
*   [!= (Not Equal)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#%3D-not-equal)
    
*   [crossover](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#crossover)
    
*   [crossunder](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#crossunder)
    
*   [cross](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#cross)
    
*   [Logical Operators](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#logical-operators)
    
*   [and](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#and)
    
*   [or](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#or)
    
*   [not](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#not)
    
*   [History Referencing Operator \[\]](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#history-referencing-operator-)
    
*   [Sequence Operators](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#sequence-operators)
    
*   [then](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#then)
    
*   [! (Inline Invalidation)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#inline-invalidation)
    

Operators are specific tokens (characters) performing an operation over multiple defined elements. Alert scripting supports three types of operators described below.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#comparison-operators)

Comparison Operators

Comparison operators are used to compare two numerical values with each other.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#%3E-greater-than)

`>` (Greater Than)

* * *

`True` if value to the left of `>` is greater than the value to its right.

Example

    {close} > {open}
    

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#%3C-less-than)

`<` (Less Than)

* * *

`True` if value to the left of `<` is less than the value to its right.

Example

    {close} < {open}
    

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#%3E=-greater-than-or-equal)

`>=` (Greater Than or Equal)

* * *

`True` if value to the left of `>=` is greater or equal to the value to its right.

Example

    {close} >= {open}
    

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#%3C=-less-than-or-equal)

`<=` (Less Than or Equal)

* * *

`True` if value to the left of `<=` is greater or equal to the value to its right.

Example

    {close} <= {open}
    

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#==-equal)

`==` (Equal)

* * *

`True` if value to the left of `==` is equal to the value to its right.

Example

    {close} == {open}
    

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#=-not-equal)

`!=` (Not Equal)

* * *

`True` if value to the left of `!=` is not equal to the value to its right.

Example

    {close} != {open}
    

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#crossover)

`crossover`

* * *

`True` if series to the left of `crossover` is crossing over the series to its right. Also expressed as:

*   `A crossover B = A > B and A[1] < B[1]`

Example

    {close} crossover {open}
    

`crossover` is not a traditional operator but serves a comparative purpose for alert scripting.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#crossunder)

`crossunder`

* * *

`True` if the series to the left of `crossunder` is crossing under the series to its right. Also expressed as:

*   `A crossunder B = A < B and A[1] > B[1]`

Example

    {close} crossunder {open}
    

`crossunder` is not a traditional operator but serves a comparative purpose for alert scripting.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#cross)

`cross`

* * *

`True` if the series to the left of `cross` is crossing (either over or under) the series to its right. Also expressed as:

*   `A cross B = A crossover B or A crossunder B`
*   `A cross B = (A - B) * (A[1] - B[1]) < 0`

Example

    {close} cross {open}
    

`cross` is not a traditional operator but serves a comparative purpose for alert scripting.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#logical-operators)

Logical Operators

Logical operators link two expressions together forming a more complex condition being either `True` or `False`.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#and)

`and`

* * *

The `and` operator return true if both expressions to its side are `True`.

Example

    {close} > {open} and {volume} > 1000
    

The above return `True` if the closing price is greater than the opening price while the volume is greater than 1000.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#or)

`or`

* * *

The `or` operator return true if either one of the expressions to its side are `True`.

Example

    {close} > {open} or {close} > {hl2}
    

The above return `True` if the closing price is greater than the opening price or if the closing price is greater than the median price `hl2`. It is important to note that `or` takes precedence over `and`, for example:

    {close} > {open} and {volume} > 1000 or {close} > {hl2} and {volume} > 1000
    

In the above condition `{close} > {open} and {volume} > 1000` and `{close} > {hl2} and {volume} > 1000` would be evaluated first.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#not)

`not`

The `not` operator test if a following condition is true or false, returning `True` if the condition is `False`.

    not {close} > {open}
    

The above return `True` if the closing price is not greater than the opening price.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#history-referencing-operator-)

History Referencing Operator `[]`

Users can refer to previous values of a series using the historical referencing operator `[]`. This operator is placed to the right of a placeholder within the curly brackets:

Syntax

    {A[n]}
    

Where `n` is a numerical value determining the number of bars back to go fetching `{A}`. For example, if we want to get the previous value of the closing price we can use `{close[1]}`.

Example

    {close} > {close[1]}
    

The above example return `True` if the current closing price is greater than value of the closing price one bar back.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#sequence-operators)

Sequence Operators

Sequence related operators allow defining and controling sequences.

A sequence is a structure made of steps. When one step is triggered we switch to the next step on the next bar.If there are no more steps to evaluate we say that the sequence is complete and start from the first step again.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#then)

`then`

* * *

Operator defining a sequence. Each condition in between `then` is a step, with the first step being the leftmost condition before `then`.

Syntax

    {a} then {b} then {c}
    

Where `{a}`, `{b}`, `{c}` are the step conditions.

Example

    {close} > {open} then {close} < {open} then {close} > {open} and {volume} > 1000
    

In the above example we have a sequence with 3 steps:

*   Step 1: `{close} > {open}` _(is the closing price greater than the open price)_
*   Step 2: `{close} < {open}` _(is the closing price lower than the open price)_
*   Step 3: `{close} > {open} and {volume} > 1000` _(is the closing price greater than the open price and volume above 1000)_

We first evaluate step 1, if it is true we will start evaluating step 2 starting at the next bar. Once step 2 is true, we will finally start evaluating step 3 sarting at the next bar. Step 3 is the last step of our sequence, once it is true the sequence will be complete and will restart evaluating from step 1 at the next bar.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/operators#inline-invalidation)

`!` (Inline Invalidation)

* * *

Operator invalidating a sequence if the assocated condition is true. Inline invalidation always takes place **before** the evaluation of a sequence step.

Invalidation reffer to restarting a sequence prematurely before it is complete.

Syntax

    {a} then {b} then {c} ! {d}
    

Where `{a}`, `{b}`, `{c}` are the step conditions and `{d}` is the invalidation condition.

Example

    {close} > {open} then {close} > {open} then {close} > {open} ! {close} < {open}
    

In the above example we have a 3 step sequence using the same conditions (closing price greater than the opening price), and an inline invalidation condition defined after the invalidation operator `!`. Before evaluating any step from the sequence, the invalidation condition will be checked first, if it is true then we reset the sequence to step 1, after this we immediately evaluate the sequence from step 1.

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

[Actions & Methods](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/alert-scripting/actions-methods)

# TP/SL | Signals & Overlays | LuxAlgo

[Skip to main content](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/tp-sl-points#content-area)

[LuxAlgo home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9a82ae47268cbdb594f7f904c8dc654f)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/logo/dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=9db2e704694ba3dd9d249afa92f16cc5)](https://docs.luxalgo.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Signals & Overlays

TP/SL Points

On this page

*   [Alerts](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/tp-sl-points#alerts)
    
*   [TP/SL Placeholders](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/tp-sl-points#tp%2Fsl-placeholders)
    

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-algo/tp-sl/settings.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=738989579023d223b79e07d17bc21e30) The TP/SL feature displays 4 take profits/stop losses levels and aims to help the user set stop losses and take profits by estimating points of potential support/resistance from an initial user-selected condition. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-algo/tp-sl/tpsl.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=d9229f428ec3a1ca10c40dffc9216951) Take-profits/stop-loss levels are based on the option selected in the “TP/SL Levels” dropdown menu. Options include the following:

| Option | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `Signals` | Will calculate new take-profits/stop-losses when a new Confirmation or Contrarian signal is detected. If the signal is bullish, take profits will be located above the price and stop losses below; if bearish, the opposite applies. |
| `Smart Trail` | Will calculate new take-profits/stop-losses when the Smart Trail turns bullish or bearish. If it turns bullish, take profits will be located above the price and stop losses below; if bearish, the opposite applies. |
| `Reversal Zones` | Will calculate new take-profits/stop-losses when the price reaches the Reversal Zones outer bands. If the price goes below the bottom zone, take profits will be located below the price and stop losses above; if the price goes above the top zone, the opposite applies. |
| `Trend Catcher` | Will calculate new take-profits/stop-losses when the Trend Catcher turns bullish or bearish. If it turns bullish, take profits will be located above the price and stop losses below; if bearish, the opposite applies. |
| `Trend Tracer` | Will calculate new take-profits/stop-losses when the Trend Tracer turns bullish or bearish. If it turns bullish, take profits will be located above the price and stop losses below; if bearish, the opposite applies. |
| `Neo Cloud` | Will calculate new take-profits/stop-losses when the Neo Cloud turns bullish or bearish. If it turns bullish, take profits will be located above the price and stop losses below; if bearish, the opposite applies. |
| `Custom Alert Creator` | Will calculate new take-profits/stop-losses when the user-set custom alert creator condition is true. |

When the price significantly deviates from the highest take profit or lowest stop loss, these will update, returning new relevant take profits and stop losses.

Users can notice when a tp/sl has updated based on where their levels start, if the levels start where the initial condition is located then it hasn’t updated.

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-algo/tp-sl/tpsl_dist.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=1962bcfd3c8bb3f497ae5500432d0f29) Users can control the distance between the price and the take profits/stop losses using the “Distance” setting, with higher values returning take profits/stop losses farther away from the price.

Make sure to adjust this setting according to the price variations you are trading. If you are trading large price variations, use a higher setting value.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/tp-sl-points#alerts)

Alerts

Users can be alerted when the price reaches a take profit or stop loss level using the “Take Profit” and/or “Stop Loss” “any alert() function call” conditions. This alert triggers once per bar.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/tp-sl-points#tp/sl-placeholders)

TP/SL Placeholders

Plots for accessing take profits and stop losses levels are available in order for users to set alerts based on them. Use the placeholder `{{plot("Take Profit")}}` for accessing the nearest take profit value and `{{plot("Stop Loss")}}` for accessing the nearest stop loss value.

_CFTC Rule 4.41 - Hypothetical or Simulated performance results have certain limitations, unlike an actual performance record, simulated results do not represent actual trading. Also, since the trades have not been executed, the results may have under-or-over compensated for the impact, if any, of certain market factors, such as lack of liquidity. Simulated trading programs in general are also subject to the fact that they are designed with the benefit of hindsight. No representation is being made that any account will or is likely to achieve profit or losses similar to those shown._

Signals & Overlays

Dashboard

On this page

*   [Dashboard Elements](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/dashboard#dashboard-elements)
    
*   [Optimal Sensitivity](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/dashboard#optimal-sensitivity)

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/dashboard/image601.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=d684ba617ce04cb100c31739d9458c36) The dashboard displays the most relevant metrics from within our premium features. This feature is extremely useful to easily obtain pertinent information regarding the market and can be used in confluence with confirmation or contrarian signals.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/dashboard#dashboard-elements)

Dashboard Elements
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/dashboard#optimal-sensitivity)

Optimal Sensitivity

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/dashboard/image576.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=6eae39afb78673f3f19eefcb85f664ae) The optimal sensitivity is an estimate of the optimal **sensitivity** setting. Depending on the selected signal mode, the recommended sensitivity for confirmation or contrarian signals will be displayed. When **None** is selected, no optimal sensitivity will be displayed. This value is obtained through grid search optimization by using the most recent 250 bars and varies in a range between 10 and 20. The cell color is based on the signal returned by the signal algorithm using the returned optimal setting, with a green color indicating a bullish signal and a red color indicating a bearish signal.

Note that this metric is not indicative of future results.

When **Autopilot Sensitivity** is enabled, the recommended sensitivity will not appear on the dashboard and is replaced with an indication notifying the user that autopilot is enabled. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/dashboard/image544.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=08d90d4916b0ee1f090aeec8d407208d)

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/dashboard#trend-strength)

Trend Strength

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/dashboard/image107.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=b07e4b1f89e6cffc17bcc745c7e9198e) The trend strength quantifies the strength of an underlying trend as a percentage and can inform the trader whether the market is trending or ranging. This indication can help a trader know whether a signal has a higher chance of being false or not. The 🔥 sign is used with trending markets while ❄️ is used for ranging markets. The cell color is based on the currently displayed signal, with a green color indicating a bullish signal and a red color indicating a sell signal. A trend strength plot is available allowing users to set alerts based on it, using placeholders `{{plot("Trend Strength"}}` in the alert message.

A percentage superior to 50% would indicate a trending market, while inferior percentages would indicate a ranging market.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/dashboard#lux-volatility)

Lux Volatility

The Lux volatility appearing on the dashboard is based on the **Lux Volatility** indicator and returns either **Stable** during periods of low volatility or **Volatile** during periods of high volatility. When volatility is rising the 📈 sign will appear, while 📉 appears when volatility is declining. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/dashboard/image585.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=c2a087df42e1a9cfafe0b1d09e880a46) The Lux volatility can also display with a warning sign, this happens when the volatility is either too low or too high and indicates extra precaution.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/dashboard#squeeze)

Squeeze

Squeeze is a measure of price compression. Higher values of this metric indicate that the market is being compressed into a tighter area, suggesting market prices are subject to damping. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/dashboard/squeeze.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=062063611c0b9e7aa806b0f2e6f00cf7) Higher values of this metric are mostly returned during ranging markets.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/dashboard#volume-sentiment)

Volume Sentiment

The volume sentiment metric returns an estimate of whether most volume came from buying or selling participants. This measure is expressed as a percentage in the range \[-100 / 100\]. ![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/dashboard/volume.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=0e5a50a00fb1a9e786b52e2f1ba01488) The value of this metric can sometimes be high or low even if a candle does not reflect this sentiment, thus potentially indicating a reversal.

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/dashboard#dashboard-settings)

Dashboard Settings
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/dashboard/image591.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=20e84268f22e7da4005421301340a22d) Enabling/disabling the dashboard can be done from the **Indicator Overlay** section. Settings affecting the dashboard visual style can be found in the **Advanced Settings** section.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/dashboard#dashboard-location)

Dashboard Location

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/dashboard/image610.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=124f76629748b0096804703a4ff1b24e) Determines the corner where the dashboard is displayed on the chart. Selecting “Hidden” will hide the dashboard.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/signals-overlays/dashboard#dashboard-size)

Dashboard Size

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4/public/images/lux-algo/dashboard/image584.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=-Cu8R2acNraf_ZS4&q=85&s=12ea8bea6f4a4ad8f5833d5a13e60648) Determines the size of the dashboard on the chart, options include **Tiny**, **Small**, **Normal**, and **Large**.

Oscillator Matrix

Alerts

*   [Any alert() Function Call](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#any-alert-function-call-2)
    

The Oscillator Matrix® can alert users for multiple events relevant to the existing features in the toolkit. To learn more about how to set alerts in general see [how to create alerts on tradingview](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/getting-started/tradingview-alerts)
.

In order for an alert to work in the toolkit make sure the related feature is enabled

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#any-alert-function-call)

Any alert() function call
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-oscillator/alerts/any-alert.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=ece1ee34db8c730d9c6734cee5302ae6)

It possible to set only one alert alerting for multiple selected conditions by the users. Conditions can be selected in the **Any alert() function call** group in the indicator settings. Then the user can set an alert by selecting “any alert() function call” as condition.

Alert conditions for the “any alert() function call” use a `once per bar close` frequency

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#any-alert-function-call-message)

Any Alert() Function Call Message

Users can set a custom message that will be used when an any alert() function call condition is triggered in the message field below the list of conditions. Users can use placeholders to customize messages and return useful information, the following placeholders are supported:

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#symbol-placeholders)

Symbol Placeholders

| Placeholder | Description | Example |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `{default}` | Default message associated with the trigerred condition | `"Bullish Divergence"` |
| `{ticker}` | Symbol ticker without the exchange prefix | `"MSFT"` |
| `{exchange}` | Symbol exchange/data source | `"COINBASE"` |
| `{sector}` | Sector of the symbol, `na` if the symbol has no sector | `"Technology Services"` |
| `{market}` | Symbol market type | `"Stocks"` |

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#time-placeholders)

Time Placeholders

| Placeholder | Description | Example |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `{tf}` | Chart timeframe, includes “S” for seconds, “D” for days, “W” for weeks, “M” for months | `"15"` |
| `{time}` | Unix time in milliseconds in exchange timezone | `"1705331385158"` |
| `{year}` | Current year in exchange timezone | `"2024"` |
| `{month}` | Current month in exchange timezone | `"7"` |
| `{day}` | Current day of the month in exchange timezone | `"21"` |

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#data-placeholders)

Data Placeholders

| Placeholder | Description | Example |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `{open}` | Opening price | `"1.2145"` |
| `{high}` | High price | `"1.2357"` |
| `{low}` | Low price | `"1.1983"` |
| `{close}` | Closing price | `"1.0569"` |
| `{volume}` | Current volume | `"45216"` |

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#indicators-placeholders)

Indicators Placeholders

| Placeholder | Description | Example |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `{moneyflow}` | Money Flow oscillator value | `"56.89"` |
| `{bull_overflow}` | Bullish Overflow value | `"51.63"` |
| `{bear_overflow}` | Bearish Overflow value | `"46.52"` |
| `{hyperwave}` | HyperWave oscillator value | `"78.44"` |
| `{hyperwave_signal}` | HyperWave oscillator signal line value | `"72.61"` |
| `{bull_confluence}` | Bullish confluence zone value. 2 if exhibiting strong confluence, 1 for weak confluence, and 0 for no confluence | `"2"` |
| `{bear_confluence}` | Bearish confluence zone value. 2 if exhibiting strong confluence, 1 for weak confluence, and 0 for no confluence | `"0"` |
| `{confluence_meter}` | Confluence meter value | `"89.73"` |

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#format-as-json)

Format as JSON

Use the following message template to receive “any alert() function call” messages in the JSON format:

    {
      "alert": "{default}",
      "ticker": "{ticker}",
      "tf": "{tf}",
      "ohlcv":{
        "open": {open},
        "high": {high},
        "low": {low},
        "close": {close},
        "volume": {volume}
      },
      "bartime": {time}
    }
    

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#custom-alert-creator)

Custom Alert Creator
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-oscillator/alerts/custom.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=a17b2090c9062d909bf9223292257852) Users wishing to construct more complex alerts using features within the toolkit and/or external indicators can use the **Custom Alert Creator**. The custom alert creator allows alerting when various user set conditions are met or when a sequence of conditions is complete.

A user wishing to be alerted when the money flow is bullish (above 50) while the HyperWave is overbought (above 80) could do it as follows:![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-oscillator/alerts/custom_example.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=91758ddbf4f3b894b753a8a5ab3ae198)

A custom alert can be triggered as an _any alert() function call_ if the setting is selected or as a regular alert when selected in the Tradingview alert creator menu.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#steps)

Steps

Steps allow creating a sequence of conditions, which when met trigger an alert. When a condition with a step equal to 1 is met the next condition associated with step 2 will be evaluated (if enabled) and so on for higher steps (if any). Conditions with the same associated step will require for both conditions to be true in order for the condition associated to a higher step (if any) to be evaluated. This allows certain conditions to act as filters.

A user wishing to be alerted when the HyperWave cross under 80 after any bearish reversal signal could do it as follows:![](https://mintcdn.com/luxalgo/fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8/public/images/lux-oscillator/alerts/step_example.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=fwDpVLIFpofJkOq8&q=85&s=b4b05c8e7545cb458eaad79315846875)

Make sure steps are set such that they form a linear sequence. For example if the lowest step is 2 or if the set steps are only 1 and 3 an error will be returned.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#or-step-operator)

OR Step Operator

The “OR” step operator can be used to get alerted for any additional condition using “OR” as step, in addition to other set custom alert conditions. Conditions using the “OR” step can be highlighted using a different color, which can be set from the Custom Alert Creator settings.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#all-step-operator)

All Step Operator

The “All” step operator can be used to filter any set “Step” condition, including “OR” and “Invalidate”. This step operator can be useful if all the steps in a sequence needs to obey a specific rule.

If a user has 2 steps set, and requires both of these to occur at a specific time interval such as 9am to 1pm, then we can use a “Session” condition using the “All” step, requiring our step 1 and step 2 to be occur between 9am and 1pm.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#invalidate-step)

Invalidate Step

The “Invalidate” step allows to set a condition as an “invalidation condition”. When this condition is triggered while a sequence of conditions is incomplete, the sequence will restart at step 1. If multiple steps are set as “Invalidate” any of the conditions being true will reset the sequence of conditions, as such not all of them are required to be true for the sequence of conditions to reset.

Example
-------

Let’s take an example where we use 2 regular steps and one “Invalidate” step. The alert will trigger when step 2 trigger after step 1 has been triggered.

1

[](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#)

Step 1

Step 1 condition trigger, we will now evaluate step 2 from now on.

2

[](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#)

Invalidation Step

Invalidation step condition trigger, we reset the sequence and evaluate step 1 just after.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#invalidation-behaviors)

Invalidation Behaviors

Invalidation behaviors allows adding more restrictions to a sequence of conditions, users can use two different invalidation behaviors described below:

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#invalidate-on-step-1)

Invalidate On Step 1

The “Invalidate On Step 1” behavior allows to reset an incomplete sequence of conditions when the condition on step 1 trigger. This prevents the first step condition from happening in between other steps of the condition sequence. This behavior is useful when the first step of our sequence of conditions needs to never be repeated during the sequence.

Example
-------

Let’s take an example where we use 3 regular steps.

1

[](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#)

Step 1

Step 1 condition trigger, we will now evaluate step 2 from now on.

2

[](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#)

Step 2

Step 2 condition trigger, we will now evaluate step 3 from now on.

3

[](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#)

Step 1 Trigger

Step 1 condition trigger, we start evaluating step 2 from now.

#### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#invalidate-on-any-repeated-step)

Invalidate On Any Repeated Step

The “Invalidate On Any Repeated Step” behavior allows to reset an incomplete sequence of conditions when a step is triggered such that it does not respect the set order of conditions. This behavior is useful when we want a perfectly ordered sequence of conditions to complete, without any step repeating itself.

Example
-------

Let’s take an example where we use 3 regular steps.

1

[](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#)

Step 1

Step 1 condition trigger, we will now evaluate step 2 from now on.

2

[](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#)

Step 2

Step 2 condition trigger, we will now evaluate step 3 from now on.

3

[](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#)

Step 1 or 2 Trigger

Step 1 or 2 conditions trigger, we start evaluating step 1 from now.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#maximum-step-interval)

Maximum Step Interval

Users can determine what is the maximum allowed horizontal distance (in bars) between two steps by enabling the “Maximum Step Interval” setting. This allows restricting steps separated by a large amount of bars. If the amount of bars since a step exceed the set threshold, then the conditions sequence is reset, and we start evaluating from step 1 again.

### 

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#highlight-on-chart)

Highlight On Chart

When a custom alert condition is set, a visual element is displayed at the bottom of the chart in order to more easily visualize when the custom alert conditions occur (displayed by default). Users can choose the location of this visual element (top, bottom of the oscillator or centered).

[​](https://docs.luxalgo.com/docs/algos/oscillator-matrix/alerts#alerts-reference)

Alerts Reference
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Pre-Set Alerts

| Alert | Description |
| --- | --- |
| HyperWave Signal Up | Triggers on the event of an HyperWave signal up |
| HyperWave OS Signal Up | Triggers on the event of an HyperWave oversold signal up |
| HyperWave Signal Down | Triggers on the event of an HyperWave signal down |
| HyperWave OB Signal Down | Triggers on the event of an HyperWave overbought signal down |
| Reversal Up | Triggers on the event of a detected reversal up signal |
| Reversal Up + | Triggers on the event of a detected reversal up + signal |
| Reversal Down | Triggers on the event of a detected reversal down signal |
| Reversal Down + | Triggers on the event of a detected reversal down + signal |
| Bullish Divergence | Triggers on the event of a detected bullish divergence |
| Bearish Divergence | Triggers on the event of a detected bearish divergence |
| Strong Bullish Confluence | Triggers when a strong bullish confluence is detected |
| Weak Bullish Confluence | Triggers when a weak bullish confluence is detected |
| Strong Bearish Confluence | Triggers when a strong bearish confluence is detected |
| Weak Bearish Confluence | Triggers when a weak bearish confluence is detected |
| Bullish Overflow | Triggers when bullish overflow is detected |
| Bearish Overflow | Triggers when bearish overflow is detected |
| Custom Alert Condition | Triggers on the event of a user set custom alert condition being true |
